## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the core problem in population dynamics. The relationship typically involves density-dependent feedback mechanisms where growth rate depends on current population size.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced per-capita growth at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * t)) (carrying capacity changing with time)
- Periodic environment: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal fluctuations in growth)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic growth with Holling type II harvesting)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth minus linear death)
- Exponential decay carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (time-dependent environmental degradation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent growth limitation → multiplicative factor (1 - P/K) or rational form 1/(1 + c*P) reflecting resource competition
- Allee effects (cooperative behavior at low density) → additional multiplicative factor (P - threshold) creating a minimum viable population
- Logarithmic density dependence → log(K/P) terms indicating Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate decreases logarithmically
- Fractional power of population → P**c with 0<c<1 indicating surface-area-to-volume scaling in organism growth
- Competing birth-death processes → difference of two power-law terms (c0*P**a - c1*P**b) representing distinct biological mechanisms
- Time-dependent environmental forcing → multiplicative modulation of growth parameters by functions of t (polynomial, periodic, or exponential)
- Ratio-dependent terms → P/(c0 + P) representing saturating functional responses in predation or resource uptake
- Per-capita growth rate as key diagnostic → dP_dt/P should reveal the density-dependence structure (linear in P for logistic, log in P for Gompertz)

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t, P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P/t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \times 78.49)$$

So the first part becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(355.72)\right)$$
$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/355.72\right)$$

This gives us:
$$f(t,P) = -0.1404 \cdot P^3/355.72 + 0.1404 \cdot P^2 \cdot (1/78.49 + 1/4.532) - 0.1404 \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

The GT has the form:
$$f(t,P) = a \cdot P^3 + b \cdot P^2 + c \cdot P + d \cdot P \cdot t^{e}$$

where $a, b, c, d, e$ are specific constants (with $e < 0$, i.e., $t^{-4.532}$).

So the GT is: **P³ term + P² term + P term + P·t^(negative power) term**

Now let me check each candidate.

### Candidate 1: P²·c0 + P·c1 + P^c2·c3·t^c4 + P^c5·c6·sin(c7·t + c8)
Has a sin(t) term. Setting c6=0 removes it, leaving P²·c0 + P·c1 + P^c2·c3·t^c4. Missing P³ term. We could set c2=3 to get P³·c3·t^c4, but then we lose the P·t^c term. We need both P³ and P·t^c. Can't do both with one power term.
Wait - we could set c5=1, c6·sin = P·t^{-4.532}? No, sin depends on t, not a power of t. We'd need c6=0 to kill the sin term. Then we have P²·c0 + P·c1 + P^c2·c3·t^c4. This can't match P³ + P² + P + P·t^e simultaneously.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: P³·c0 + P²·c1 + P·c2/(P+c3) + P·c4·t^c5 + P·c6·exp(c7·t)
Set c6=0 to kill exp term. Then: P³·c0 + P²·c1 + P·c2/(P+c3) + P·c4·t^c5.
P·c2/(P+c3) = c2·P/(P+c3). With common denominator: c2·P/(P+c3).
GT needs P² + P + P·t^e + P³. We have P³ + P² + P·c2/(P+c3) + P·t^c5.
P·c2/(P+c3) = c2 - c2·c3/(P+c3). This introduces a term 1/(P+c3) which doesn't exist in GT. Set c2=0, then we have P³·c0 + P²·c1 + P·c4·t^c5. Missing the linear P term.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]
